### Post by TehBleachBottle on 2009-04-30
I had been in the middle of installing quite a few new applications into 9.04 and the panels dissapeared and an Eagle program if I remeber correctly, popped up. After clicking next and closing it out I thought the desktop would return to it's normal state. It didn't. Did right click to see if I could add the panels back and everything put no, nothing came up. Tried the right click button and nothing happened either. Restarted still nothing. I'm guessing one one the many applications I installed is the root of the problem. I don't know if it matters but the Synaptic package manager was in the middle of configuring the packages.
 So... what should I do? :confused:

---

### Post by codeseer on 2009-04-30
What type of new applications? You are using Ubuntu?

See if hitting CTRL+ALT+F5 gets you a console. You can switch back by hitting CTRL+ALT+F7.

---

I would say what I had exactly installed but I don't remember all of them. I am big on possibilities. And if you can't tell I can't very well navigate myself through command line well. ### Post by codeseer on 2009-05-05
I'd try:

```

apt-get clean
apt-get remove nvidia-180-modaliases
apt-get update
apt-get install nvidia-180-modaliases
apt-get check

```

### Post by codeseer on 2009-05-06
> **TehBleachBottle said:**
> Actually I've done manual every single time since I first installed Ubuntu a month or two ago and every single reinstall afterward I have used manual partitioning (I was paranoid that it would ruin the my cp or my vista partition) Actually do you know if it possible to reassign the /usr to be back in / or to just get gparted to do its job in a small period of time, because it always seems to take so long. I usual end up closing it out even when it says that it may cause an error (my reasoning is that the partition only hold videos which I have backed up already).

If that's the case, you can probably just copy the contents over to /usr in the root directory and ditch the /usr partition and edit /etc/fstab. You could download a gparted live cd, but I doubt it would be much faster.
